<div id="review_2270793713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2270793713" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2270793713?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525555384" href="/book/show/15837671-turtles-all-the-way-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=book-heaven">book-heaven</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2270793713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5840887710541734536">bf: *gets me a book*<br/>bf: *picks this one because there's 'turtles' in the title*<br/><br/>____________________________________<br/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>No one ever says goodbye unless they want to see you again.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/>I must admit that never in a million years, would have expected to find myself in a situation like this, one where I'd end up completely put off guard by a book I'd never even considered reading in the first place.<br/>I'm not a huge John Green fan. I've read his previous works and, even if I didn't completely despise them, t</span>
  <span id="freeText5840887710541734536" style="display:none">bf: *gets me a book*<br>bf: *picks this one because there's 'turtles' in the title*<br><br>____________________________________<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>No one ever says goodbye unless they want to see you again.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br>I must admit that never in a million years, would have expected to find myself in a situation like this, one where I'd end up completely put off guard by a book I'd never even considered reading in the first place.<br>I'm not a huge John Green fan. I've read his previous works and, even if I didn't completely despise them, the whole JG phenomenon never really felt to me like a complete mind-blowing experience that I absolutely had to be part of.<br><br>Then why does this book changes the entire game, you might ask? <br>Well, first of all, there was a lot to relate to. And I'm not only talking about all those pop-culture references and the exquisitely colloquial writings. I mean, yes, they're quite necessary if you look at it from a certain angle, and they serve their filling purpose greatly, but it's something else, really. <br>As simple as it sounds, I found myself utterly and painfully represented by the issues this book portraits, and I couldn't help but see my own fight against the same angsty and suffocating thoughts the main character, Aza, has to struggle with on a daily basis, as well.<br>It's really something that doesn't happen everyday. <br>Aza is a complex and damaged character, one of those charries I usually am drawn to, only this time it was because her character sometimes appeared very adult-coded, so it was a case of mutual and shared vision of life. <br>Through the pages, you get to see her journey, in and outside her head, and, I don't know if it's just me being me, but some of the things she does and says are things I thought I was the only one doing. <br>Talk about relatable MC's! I like her, so so so so much. <br>Green's characters once again fall a bit on the cliché side, but I got to give it to him. When they start throwing tantrums, I don't blame them, because they're young and immature, just like they should be. <br>And when they learn from their mistakes, is even better. <br>Aza's mum is probably the purest character I've seen in years. She's adorable. I respect the shit out of that woman, I admire her for being so strong and for keeping herself together for her daughter's sake even when things are shitty. She's a good mum and a good role model. <br>Love interests aren't usually a problem for me, except for when they become love-interests-period. This time around, it was Davis' turn and, I've got to say it, I adore the guy. <br>Just like Aza, he's walking a wire, with one foot dangling from the edge of the darker side, constrantly fighting to live up to a family name he didn't choose himself. <br>And he's so... Likeable, you know? At least for me. <br>I mean, he's got this whole Gansey thing going on (cute and nerdy rich boy, wears khakis and polo shirts, has a frigging diary) and he loves poetry. No, let me rephrase that: he loves and <b>writes</b> poetry. <br>*sticks gold star on davis forehead*<br><br><br>Back to us...<br>So, reason #3 this book is the best I've read this month: the plot is so blunt and easy to follow, that it flows perfectly with whatever mood you might be in that moment. Sure, it's not the thriller of the year nor the best contemporary that deals with heavy themes, but if you put all the elements together and follow the recipe step by step, you're in for an adventure.<br>The quotes sprinkled all over the book, in a certified Green fashion, the very same quotes I've always found a bit pretentious in the other books, add a sense of poetry (as if there was little of it already! *puts another gold star on davis forehead*), a sense of being known. <br><br>The romance is light but at the same time very intense. It's not even that much eye-rolling, if you know what I mean. <br>Some Davis/Aza scenes really left me out of breath, not gonna lie, but I really did like Aza and Daisy's interactions just as much. I speak from personal experience when I say it's not easy being friends with people who have social anxiety and/or ocd (especially since they, <i>we</i>, take a little more than others to open up to people and let them in), so I appreciate the author's effort of showing how relationships and dynamics can work out with a little help from both sides. And it's not always sunshine and rainbows, that be clear. I also think Green does an amazing job at presenting you both sides of the medal, backstabbing and wishful thinking included.<br><br>I think this was the first time in ages I had to physically keep myself from reading an entire novel in one day, because I didn't want it to end too soon. <br>I'm glad I found, in this unexpected surprise of a book, a story that made me feel a little less alone in the world.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5840887710541734536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11459431494098307128">“no one ever says good-bye unless they want to see you again. aa”<br/><br/>ever since I finished this book, this sentence has been in my mind, and I've been going over it, again and again, trying to grasp its full meaning. I found out that there's a Japanese word "Sayonara" which means final good-bye. It's not something that you say to someone you are sure you're gonna see again. From my understanding, it also means that if we meet again, we'll be different people, I'll be a different person. And it makes</span>
  <span id="freeText11459431494098307128" style="display:none">“no one ever says good-bye unless they want to see you again. aa”<br /><br />ever since I finished this book, this sentence has been in my mind, and I've been going over it, again and again, trying to grasp its full meaning. I found out that there's a Japanese word "Sayonara" which means final good-bye. It's not something that you say to someone you are sure you're gonna see again. From my understanding, it also means that if we meet again, we'll be different people, I'll be a different person. And it makes sense, it makes so much sense.<br /><br />“Your now is not your forever.”</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2395739732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395739732" />
    <a title="Bill Gates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62787798-bill-gates"><img alt="Bill Gates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603744542p2/62787798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395739732?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Gates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Gates" href="/user/show/62787798-bill-gates">Bill Gates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395739732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6947935802414605551">When Melinda and I did an event with John Green in New York a couple years ago, we knew we had to bring our youngest daughter, Phoebe, along. He is one of her favorite authors, and she’s converted our entire family to fans of his books.<br/><br/>Before we went on stage, John pulled Phoebe aside to share a secret with her: the plot of his new book. He made her promise not to share it with anyone, and she stayed true to her word for nearly two years. She wouldn’t even tell Melinda and me!<br/><br/>Phoebe doesn’t have</span>
  <span id="freeText6947935802414605551" style="display:none">When Melinda and I did an event with John Green in New York a couple years ago, we knew we had to bring our youngest daughter, Phoebe, along. He is one of her favorite authors, and she’s converted our entire family to fans of his books.<br /><br />Before we went on stage, John pulled Phoebe aside to share a secret with her: the plot of his new book. He made her promise not to share it with anyone, and she stayed true to her word for nearly two years. She wouldn’t even tell Melinda and me!<br /><br />Phoebe doesn’t have to keep the secret any longer, because that book—<i>Turtles All the Way Down</i>—was released late last year.<br /><br />I’ve read a couple of John’s books and enjoyed each one, and his latest is no exception. Turtles All the Way Down tells the story of Aza Holmes, a high school student from Indianapolis. When a local billionaire goes missing and a $100,000 reward is offered for information about his disappearance, she and her best friend decide to track him down.<br /><br />Aza’s quest is complicated by the fact that she has obsessive compulsive disorder and severe anxiety. Her struggles are a huge part of the book, as her compulsions constantly get in the way of her social life. John’s writing feels almost claustrophobic when describing Aza’s mental swirl. Some people might find those parts difficult to read, but he really gives you a sense of what it feels like to live with OCD.<br /><br />Because this is a John Green novel, romance must factor into the equation. Aza begins to develop feelings for Davis, the son of missing billionaire Russell Pickett. He is initially skeptical about her intentions, because he’s used to people sucking up to him to get close to his dad. While I hope I’m nothing like the morally bankrupt Russell—he wants to give all of his money to his pet lizard and was under investigation for fraud and bribery—I think my own kids can relate to some of Davis’ experiences.<br /><br />John actually talked to Phoebe in New York about what it was like growing up with me as her dad. I asked her to write up her own mini-review now that’s she had a chance to read the book. Here’s what Phoebe had to say:<br /><br />“For years I have been a loyal John Green fan—devouring his novels in the back of coffee shops, while traveling, and curled up on my couch. Something about the imagery of his books makes me get caught up in the fantasy of his stories, but <i>Turtles All the Way Down</i> hit closer to home for me than the rest. As someone who has struggled with OCD for years, I saw some of myself in the main character. But more than anything, this book struck close to home due to the intriguing character of Davis.<br /><br />“Never has a book been able to capture so well what it is like to live in the shadow of someone else’s legacy. This story shows how Davis struggled to find his own identity outside of his father’s fame and wealth. Although we have very different relationships with our dads, I recognized his struggle, which also plays into my own life as I find my way in this world. This read was captivating like none other I have read before.”<br /><br />Phoebe is much closer to John’s intended demographic than I am, but I think readers of all ages will enjoy <i>Turtles All the Way Down</i>. It’s a fun, moving story filled with quirky but relatable characters. <i>Paper Towns</i> is still my favorite John Green book—but my family loved talking about <i>Turtles</i> at the dinner table, and I think yours will, too.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6947935802414605551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2116467854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2116467854" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2116467854?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2116467854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6023689840333284688"><em>“If only I were as good at life as I am at the internet.”</em><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517184419ra/24956686.gif' width='“450”' height='“250”' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I was so overly eager for any new John Green book related content that I made the mistake of reading the excerpt shared on <a href='https://www.buzzfeed.com/johngreenauthor/turtles-all-the-way-down?utm_term=.qtbDADyYWO#.ijyjojegpq' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buzzfeed</a> last month. I say mistake because when I opened up the book weeks after having read the first two chapters, I only had this vague recollection that certainly wouldn't help to continue from where I'd started. Rereading was key.<br/><br/>To give you a bit more background on why I was so eager: Back in 2014, John Green was</span>
  <span id="freeText6023689840333284688" style="display:none"><em>“If only I were as good at life as I am at the internet.”</em><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517184419ra/24956686.gif" width="“450”" height="“250”" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I was so overly eager for any new John Green book related content that I made the mistake of reading the excerpt shared on <a href="https://www.buzzfeed.com/johngreenauthor/turtles-all-the-way-down?utm_term=.qtbDADyYWO#.ijyjojegpq" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buzzfeed</a> last month. I say mistake because when I opened up the book weeks after having read the first two chapters, I only had this vague recollection that certainly wouldn't help to continue from where I'd started. Rereading was key.<br><br>To give you a bit more background on why I was so eager: Back in 2014, John Green was one of the first authors I'd read that introduced me to the magic of books. I owe a lot to his writing that sucked me in so completely, only to leave me craving for more by the last page, which then led me to look up what next book would satisfy that particular hunger. And here we are today.<br><br>Despite all the above, I still went into <strong>Turtles All the Way Down</strong> with little to no expectations as to what was to come. I knew that though I had history with TFIOS, when I look back on certain scenes, I can't help but feel shivers of disgust (like when the <a href="http://motherhenna.tumblr.com/post/75224698822/why-i-dislike-the-fault-in-our-stars" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">"two very privileged caucasian Americans who have never known starvation, genocide, or physical abuse"</a> kissed in the Anne Frank house, which Ariane tells like it is in <a href="https://www.buzzfeed.com/arianelange/anne-frank-the-fault-in-our-stars?utm_term=.obABZbKWo3#.bpZdDz50J1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">this article</a>). So if anything, I was apprehensive as to what this newest work would contain.<br><br>It all begins with a fugitive billionaire and the promise of a cash reward. <strong>Turtles All the Way Down</strong> is about lifelong friendship, the intimacy of an unexpected reunion, Star Wars fan fiction, and tuatara. But at its heart is Aza Holmes, a young woman navigating daily existence within the ever-tightening spiral of her own thoughts.<br><br>I feel like the only way I can accurately describe the heart of the book is by borrowing <a href="http://www.firsttoread.com/Books/BookDetails.aspx?id=813370&amp;rid=0a54f304-1759-413c-874b-9ab2fdcbb964&amp;st=2" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">this phrase</a>: Captures the everyday moments of teens' lives and then sets fire to those moments, heightening them until they become metaphor.<br><br><em>“True terror isn’t being scared; it’s not having a choice in the matter.”</em><br><br>I have so much my mind is eager to spit out, so I think a list is in order (<b>mild spoilers ahead</b>):<br><br>• Let's start with Aza, who surprised me so much with her strong will and great depth of character. Her thought process and spirals gave me a keen insight into the works of the mind and expanding my view on things. What I wasn't expecting, however, was having my own thoughts staring back at me from the page. From staring down the rabbit hole that is social media stalking your crush (#exposed), to vocalizing my exact fears on the reality of dating:<br><br><em>“I’m really not looking to date anyone.” I know people often say that when secretly looking for a romantic partner, but I meant it. I definitely felt attracted to some people, and I liked the idea of being with someone, but the actual mechanics of it didn’t much suit my talents. Like, parts of typical romantic relationships that made me anxious included 1. Kissing; 2. Having to say the right things to avoid hurt feelings; 3. Saying more wrong things while trying to apologize; 4. Being at a movie theater together and feeling obligated to hold hands even after your hands become sweaty and the sweat starts mixing together; and 5. The part where they say, “What are you thinking about?” And they want you to be, like, “I’m thinking about you, darling,” but you’re actually thinking about how cows literally could not survive if it weren’t for the bacteria in their guts, and how that sort of means that cows do not exist as independent life-forms, but that’s not really something you can say out loud, so you’re ultimately forced to choose between lying and seeming weird.”</em><br><br>• Green’s style has grown and matured a lot for me with his newest work. It’s equal parts dark, hilarious, and achingly real. Plus, the dialogue is amazing. Speaking of the latter, the main reason why is thanks to the effervescent Daisy, who's a force to be reckoned with, from writing her own Rey/ Chewbacca fanfiction to her inspiring directness.<br><br><em>“Have you ever gotten a dick pic?” she asked in lieu of saying hello.</em><br><br>I feel like she and Ilana Wexler would get along perfectly. Actually, I've never been surer of something.<br><br><em>“I mean, how am I supposed to react to a semi-erect penis as fan mail? Am I supposed to feel intrigued?”</em><br><em>“He probably thinks it’ll end in marriage. You’ll meet IRL and fall in love and someday tell your kids that it all started with a picture of a disembodied penis.”</em><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507750494i/24145465.png" alt="tumblr_inline_ovwvvl3htk1tsgfd5_540" width="385" height="290" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>John Green isn’t afraid to let loose with his newest work. And I’m digging it.<br><br>• Speaking of which, the direction the author took with Aza's mental illness felt like the most honest portrayal I'd read in ages.<br><br><em>“I wanted to tell her that I was getting better, because that was supposed to be the narrative of illness: It was a hurdle you jumped over, or a battle you won. Illness is a story told in the past tense.”</em><br>...<br><em>“I would always be like this, always have this within me. There was no beating it. I would never slay the dragon, because the dragon was also me. My self and the disease were knotted together for life.”</em><br><br>• I got educated on such a vast array of topics, without ever feeling like I was lectured. The random history and science lessons really give away who the author of this novel is. From the history of Indianapolis (the setting of the book), to the genetically distinct creature called tuatara, to this weird parasite called Diplostomum pseudospathaceum. I can't deny how utterly fascinating John Green made all of his swift lessons.<br><br><em>“What I love about science is that as you learn, you don’t really get answers. You just get better questions.”</em><br><br>• The bits of romance seemed slightly off-kilter with the flow of the story at first, but it just so happened that I was in the rare mood for a budding romance to indulge in. Actually, it turned out to be quite nice, since it first and foremost focused on two teens taking comfort in talking with someone that gets them to a whole new level.<br><br><em>“In the best conversations, you don’t even remember what you talked about, only how it felt.”</em><br><br>• The fact that we get to read inserts from Davis's blog post &amp; poetry entries, and Daisy's successful fanfiction. The particular Davis piece below rang in my ear for a very long time.<br><br><em>“The next one stopped me cold:</em><br><br><strong>
  <em>“The greatest weapon against stress is our ability to choose one thought over another.”</em>
</strong><br><strong>
  <em>—WILLIAM JAMES</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>I don’t know what superpower William James enjoyed, but I can no more choose my thoughts than choose my name.</em>
</strong><br><br><em>The way he talked about thoughts was the way I experienced them—not as a choice but as a destiny. Not a catalog of my consciousness, but a refutation of it.</em><br><em>When I was little, I used to tell Mom about my invasives, and she would always say, “Just don’t think about that stuff, Aza.” But Davis got it. You can’t choose. That’s the problem.”</em><br><br>• On a totally separate note, I couldn't help but think of Richard Campbell Gansey III from <a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com/2016/04/17/review-the-raven-boys-by-maggie-stiefvater/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> when Davis was first introduced, thanks to his obscene amount of family money.<br><br><em>“You mean, when a movie comes out in theaters, it . . . also comes out at your house?”</em><br><br>I never thought we’d have someone upstage Gansey... And yet here we are.<br><br>• But what came quite unexpectedly was how connected I felt to Noah, who's the 13-year-old brother. We see him truly struggle with the fact that his dad up-and-left with no clue of his whereabouts. But what hit most was the fact that Noah had no one to cry out to. Davis is barely getting by on his own, so his younger brother has to figure things out mainly by himself. And reading that just took a piece right off me.<br><br><em>“It’s all right to be scared, Noah.” And then he turned his face away from me and started sobbing. “You’re okay,” I told him, lying. “You’re okay. He’ll come home.”</em><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472201424i/20164163.png" width="500" height="43" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Though the premise is set to be about making “connections that crack open the long-dormant case of Russell Pickett’s disappearance,” <strong>Turtles All the Way Down </strong>is at its core a character-driven novel, favoring the development of the characters' relationships with one another, which is how I like 'em. All this to say: I'm beyond eager to see what Green has next in store for us.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519483221i/25115431.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <em>Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</em>
</i> <strong>Turtles All the Way Down</strong>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0525555366/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=0525555366&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=50876d53fc9587896f3f5db5c2d4511b" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507750494i/24145466.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507750494i/24145467.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2017">gr_awards_2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150614343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5139551658484794014">This book was a fun audiobook experience as my wife and I listened to about 45 minutes of it together every night. I think this is a great activity for book loving spouses! <br/><br/>Partway through this book I thought I was going to give it an "okay, but didn't really blow me away" 3 stars. However, I think that the last 3rd of the book really brought things together in an interesting way.<br/><br/>At first, the book seemed like it was trying to be too many things at once. <a href='https://youtu.be/5Ny8abK6IkM' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here for a video from my Goodreads </a></span>
  <span id="freeText5139551658484794014" style="display:none">This book was a fun audiobook experience as my wife and I listened to about 45 minutes of it together every night. I think this is a great activity for book loving spouses! <br><br>Partway through this book I thought I was going to give it an "okay, but didn't really blow me away" 3 stars. However, I think that the last 3rd of the book really brought things together in an interesting way.<br><br>At first, the book seemed like it was trying to be too many things at once. <a href="https://youtu.be/5Ny8abK6IkM" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here for a video from my Goodreads friend Hannah</a> and go to 7:16 - she does a great job describing how this book is many different things. However, after finishing the book and showing the video to my wife, we agree that whether it is intentional or not, the many different directions this book goes is a great representation of the anxiety of the main character.<br><br>Another thing that really raised my enjoyment of this book is that the entirety of the events take place within about 20 minutes of my house. Also, almost every major landmark described in the book can be seen from my office window. When a book hits that close to home, it means a bit more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The entrance to Pogues Run is 5 miles from my office <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>A comparison - tell me if you agree. A John Green teenage conversation:<br><br><b>Girl: My heart is torn asunder with thoughts of my most eloquent yet deeply morose love interest. He is so elegantly handsome, but very humble because:<br><br>A. He is an artist<br>B. He is extremely wealthy but loves the simple things like fast food and independent rock music<br>C. He is misunderstood <br>D. Or, because every JG novel has lists!<br><br>Boy: You can overcome yourself with my constant caring. I immediately like you and would die for you even though we have nothing in common. Look up into the sky and behold Ursa Major, Casseopea, and Polaris as they cross the zenith of Saturn. Later I will read you the poem I wrote about this inspired by the works of William Shakespeare.</b><br><br>A teenage conversation when I was a teenager.<br><br><b>Girl: 'Sup?<br><br>Boy: 'Sup? Wanna go out?<br><br>Girl: Ewww!<br><br>Boy: 'Kay, whatever!<br><br>The End</b><br><br>Last, but not least, the Tuatara (read the book, it will make sense)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1510631693i/24436218.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3108550794" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3108550794" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3108550794?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3108550794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9761820039714053052"><i>”One of the challenges with pain – physical or psychic – is that we can really only approach it through metaphor. It can’t be represented the way a table or a body can. In some ways, pain is the opposite of language.”</i><br/><br/>Those words rang so true and I think this is my favourite quote from the entire book. Because yes, I’ve been there and done that and in all honesty I can’t tell you what was worse. Physical or psychic? In both cases I couldn’t find my voice. For different reasons but the outcome was</span>
  <span id="freeText9761820039714053052" style="display:none"><i>”One of the challenges with pain – physical or psychic – is that we can really only approach it through metaphor. It can’t be represented the way a table or a body can. In some ways, pain is the opposite of language.”</i><br /><br />Those words rang so true and I think this is my favourite quote from the entire book. Because yes, I’ve been there and done that and in all honesty I can’t tell you what was worse. Physical or psychic? In both cases I couldn’t find my voice. For different reasons but the outcome was the same. So I totally agree with this statement. Pain IS the opposite of language and if you want to work through it you’ve to learn to express yourself. <br /><br />Which is exactly what Aza is doing in this book. Or to be completely honest: This is what everyone is trying to do in this book. No matter if it’s Davis, Aza’s mom or her best friend Daisy. They all hurt, in different ways, for different reasons, but they feel pain and they really try their best to deal with it. With varying success, but they are fighting and this is always good because this means that none of them gave up yet. <br /><br /><b>“Turtles All the Way Down”</b> is no fast read, it’s neither suspenseful nor easy, but it’s real and true and this makes all the difference. You won’t find action scenes or plot twists in here, you’ll find real people with real problems and the will to work through them. No supernatural obstacles, just ordinary life and its challenges. Which, truth be told are sometimes even worse than everything a superhero has to put up with. ;-) This said, let’s head to my character section and go into more detail.<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>This is my characters section so this means that you’ll be spoiled relentlessly if you decide to continue to read. It’s your choice and up to you, but if you didn’t read the book yet and begin to regret your own curiosity: Don’t say I didn’t warn you. Because, well, I just officially did! ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Aza:</b><br /><br /><i>”And if you can’t pick what you do or think about, then maybe you aren’t really real, you know? Maybe I’m just a lie that I’m whispering to myself.”</i><br /><br />Oh, how I felt with Aza when I read this book. She knows she has a problem and she’s doing her best to work through it but she just can’t escape what she thinks or who she truly is. There’s always something gnawing at the back of her mind and even though she’s living an ordinary life and doing homework etc. there’s still something that’s holding her back. I have to admit, sometimes it was really tough to read Aza’s POV because her spirals were pretty intense. There were moments I had to close the book and put it aside… a privilege Aza didn’t have because it was her own mind and her own thoughts that haunted her. Yet despite everything she was going to school and trying to fit into our world. And sometimes she even succeeded to live in the moment. I can’t even fathom how difficult this must have been but I’m kind of proud of Aza because she never gave up. =)<br /><br /><i>”You don’t actually want to do this; it’s just an invasive. Everyone has them. But you can’t shut yours up. Since you’ve had a reasonable amount of cognitive behavioral therapy, you tell yourself, I am not my thoughts, even though deep down you’re not sure what exactly that makes you.”</i><br /><br /><b>Daisy:</b><br /><br /><i>”But a human woman falling in love with a Wookie, God forbid. I mean, I know I’m just feeding the trolls here, Holmesy, but I can’t stand for it.”</i> <br /><br />Haha! Okay, the idea of Rey/Chewie fanfic is still something I have to get used to, but in general I got the gist of what Daisy meant. *lol* I liked Aza’s best friend and it was great to see how they worked together. Daisy was definitely the outgoing and honest kind of type and I really appreciated that about her. She didn’t mince her words and never beat about the bush and this was really refreshing. I can understand why some people might think that Daisy was selfish and self-centred, but I think that she only wanted the best for Aza and really loved her. If you don’t have OCD it’s hard to understand the actions of people that have it, but Daisy tried and that has to count for something! <br /><br /><b>Davis Pickett:</b><br /><br /><i>”I don’t know what superpower William James enjoyed, but I can no more choose my thoughts than choose my name.”</i><br /><br />Where to start with Davis? What a pure and tortured soul! T_T I really loved that boy! In the eyes of others he might have had everything he wished for but Davis was aware that he didn’t have the one thing that truly counts: A loving father who took care of his sons. After his father’s disappearance he was left to his own devices and even though it seemed like everything was secured – at least legally – this didn’t change anything about the fact that he had a hard fate. Without their father and without a mother he was the only one his younger brother could rely on and this was a lot of responsibility for such a young boy. The scene where Aza’s mother confronted him and told him that she only wants the best for her daughter was so sad to read. No wonder Davis cried. If his father would have only cared about him half as much… &gt;_&lt; Davis is such a precious bean and he deserves the world! I really hope he was able to start a new life and that he got everything he wanted and more! &lt;333<br /><br /><i>”At this point I don’t care why someone likes me. I’m just so goddamned lonely. I know that’s pathetic. But yeah.”</i><br /><br /><i>He started to say something, but then had to stop, because his eyes were welling up with tears. “Davis, are you all right?” my mom asked. He tried to speak again but it devolved into a choked sob.<br />“Davis, I’m sorry, I didn’t realize….”<br />Blushing, he said, “I’m sorry.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I guess at some point, you realize that whoever takes care of you is just a person, and that they have no superpowers and can’t actually protect you from getting hurt. Which is one thing. But Noah is starting to understand that maybe the person he thought was a superhero turns out sort of to be the villain. And that really sucks.”</i><br /><br /><i>”The worst part of being truly alone is you think about all the times you wished that everyone would just leave you be. Then they do, and you are left being, and you turn out to be terrible company.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Aza &amp; Davis:</u><br /><br /><i>”Him: And the thing is, when you lose someone, you realize you’ll eventually lose everyone.<br />Me: True. And once you know that, you can never forget it.”</i><br /><br />*sighs* Those two. They would have been good for each other but their circumstances made it so difficult to be together. Aza was fighting hard against her growing OCD and Davis was kind of fighting for his and his brother’s existence. So definitely not the right time to start a relationship. Still, I liked that they were there for each other whenever things got tough and in their own way they understood and respected each other more than anyone else would have been able to. Their deep conversations were definitely the highlight of this book and I felt really sorry for both of them. It didn’t surprise me that Davis was hurt when Aza decided to break up with him, but considering their circumstances it was the sensible thing to do. This said my heart will always bleed for those two and I don’t think it will ever stop! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”I’m not gonna un-have this is what I mean. I’ve had it since I can remember and it’s not getting better and I can’t have a normal life if I can’t kiss someone without freaking out.”<br />“It’s okay, Aza. Really.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He kept saying what do I do, what do I do, his head on my shoulder. I wondered whether it was a mistake to tell him. What do I do? He asked it again and again, pleading.”</i><br /><br /><u>Daisy &amp; Aza:</u><br /><br /><i>”I don’t mean that you’re a bad friend or anything. But you’re slightly tortured, and the way you’re tortured is sometimes also painful for, like, everyone around you.”</i><br /><br />Now that was quite a friendship and I could relate to it from Daisy’s POV. I have a few friends that have OCD and even though I’m trying to understand them it’s not always easy. If you don’t have OCD it’s kinda tough to understand why people would do certain things and I think John Green portrayed this incomprehension quite well. Daisy loved Aza and this was more than just obvious, yet she still had troubles to maintain their friendship. I think most of that is due to the fact that the most ordinary things (in our eyes ordinary, mind you) become a challenge for people with OCD. We can’t even fathom what it means to go out into the world and to live with that voice in the back of your mind. So at times this makes it hard to comprehend Aza’s actions. Despite all that Daisy did everything she could. She tried to understand Aza and she accepted her the way she was. If you ask me this is what true friendship is about and in my eyes they were perfect! =) <br /><br /><i>”What are their jobs? When was the last time you were at my apartment – five years ago? We’re supposed to be best friends, Holmesy, and you don’t even know if I have any fucking pets. You have no idea what it’s like for me, and you’re so like, pathologically uncurious that you don’t even know what you don’t know.”</i><br /><br /><u>Aza &amp; her mom:</u><br /><br /><i>”You feeling scared?”<br />“Kinda.”<br />“Of what?”<br />“It’s not like that. The sentence doesn’t have, like, an object. I’m just scared.”<br />“I don’t know what to say, Aza. I see the pain on your face and I want to take it from you.”</i> <br /><br />Aza’s mom was so great! She was a single mom and tried her best to give Aza everything she needed. There was no doubt that she loved her daughter dearly and it was so good to see that she always managed to engage Aza in dialogue. Of course this wasn’t always welcome from Aza’s side but I guess that’s a typical teen trait. Regardless of their troubles and fears, no teen seems to be keen on the idea of talking with their parents about the real important things. *lol* I think that if she would have wanted to, Aza knew that she could always confide in her mother though. And last but not least her mom’s words resonated so much with me. It’s so hard to see your kid in pain and not to be able to do anything against it and if I could, I would do everything possible to take away my child’s pain. No matter if it’s heartache or a flu. XD<br /><br /><i>”You seemed locked inside of your mind, and I can’t know what’s going on in there, and it scares me.” I pressed my thumbnail against my fingertip through the Band-Aid, thinking it would scare her a lot more if she could see what was going on in there.</i><br /><br /><b>The OCD rep:</b><br /><br /><i>”The thing about a spiral is, if you follow it inward, it never actually ends. It just keeps tightening, infinitely.”</i><br /><br />I don’t have OCD so you have to take my words with a grain of salt. I do think that the rep was done very well in this book though. As I mentioned before, I have a couple of friends that suffer from OCD and before I read this book I was trying to understand them but never truly did. I think to read <b>“Turtles All the Way Down”</b> gave me a better understanding of their troubles and fears. Of course there are different types of OCD and there was only one part of it represented in here, the “thought spiral” is something that all of my friends seem to have in common though. I can’t even imagine how tough it must be to get out of bed and to live your life with thoughts like that always spinning in the back of your mind. To read about it made it so palpable and real. It’s one thing if people try to explain it to you, it’s an entirely different thing if you’re in their head and experience those things exactly like they do. Some of those book scenes were pretty intense and yes, I admit it, I sometimes found myself closing the book because I couldn’t take the repetitive thoughts and the spiral downwards any longer. When I needed a break I could close the book, but people who have OCD can’t just close a book, they have to live through their thoughts and that’s actually pretty scary. I think I finally got how scary it actually is! So thank you John Green for giving us this rep and for helping us to understand the people we love and care about! If not entirely, at least a little bit better.<br /><br /><i>”True terror isn’t being scared; it’s not having a choice in the matter.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br /><b>“Turtles All the Way Down”</b> was a fairly slow-paced and somehow gentle book. John Green dealt with quite a few sensitive topics yet always tackled them in a careful manner. Whilst it can be argued that the plot around the missing billionaire is only background music, there is no doubt that Green used it as a device in order to focus on the important things. The things that have moved our world for centuries. Love, hope, fear, anger, frustration, despair and the entire bandwidth of human emotions. If you’re looking for one or all of those things you’ll certainly gain something from reading this book! Happy reading! <br />___________________________<br /><br />I thought long and hard about which book should be the last one I start in 2019 and I eventually decided for this one. <br /><br />Many of my friends loved it and others, well…they gave it 3 stars so I guess they weren't really persuaded by it. *lol*<br />Since I love to form my own opinion I’m always ready to read a controversial book though.<br /><br />Let’s find out if I’ll like it or not. ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9761820039714053052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2306354096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword"><img alt="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603584262p2/28146945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2306354096?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword" href="/user/show/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword">Sara➽ Ink Is My Sword</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=character-driven-story">character-driven-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=forgetable">forgetable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=overhyped">overhyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=not-for-my-taste">not-for-my-taste</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28146945-sara-ink-is-my-sword?shelf=boring">boring</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2306354096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7133387133455925925"><b>1.5 “John Green is definitely a miss for me” Stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Reading someone’s poetry is like seeing them naked”</i>
</blockquote><br/><i> UHU. I just bumped to 2 stars because I am reading a 1-star book right now and this is not at that level. I can truly appreciate the OCD representation in Aza so yeah let's leave it at 1.5 near 2.</i><br/><br/>➽<u>
  <b>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED.</b>
</u><br/><br/>My problem was expectations. I thought I would relate, I didn’t. My problem was feeling. I thought I would feel, I couldn't. <br/><br/><b>JG fans please don't throw tomatoes at me. A</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7133387133455925925" style="display:none"><b>1.5 “John Green is definitely a miss for me” Stars</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Reading someone’s poetry is like seeing them naked”</i>
</blockquote><br /><i> UHU. I just bumped to 2 stars because I am reading a 1-star book right now and this is not at that level. I can truly appreciate the OCD representation in Aza so yeah let's leave it at 1.5 near 2.</i><br /><br />➽<u>
  <b>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED.</b>
</u><br /><br />My problem was expectations. I thought I would relate, I didn’t. My problem was feeling. I thought I would feel, I couldn't. <br /><br /><b>JG fans please don't throw tomatoes at me. Although if you throw them with parmesan cheese or mozzarella cheese, I may, just may be okay with it. </b><br /><br /><b>Do I think everyone will hate this book?</b> Hell, no.<br />I for sure know many people will be able to relate and enjoy this book. So don’t feel discouraged to pick this up if you want to. <i>There was nothing wrong, yet everything was wrong for me as a reader.</i><br /><b>Do I recommend it? </b>Yes, if you are a usual JG fan and if you are interested in reading more OCD representation. <br /><br />OCD representation, yes hell yes, I am glad his book exists. Many people could relate, many had this book piercing their heart, so yes I currently think what the hell is wrong with me.<s> I have the theory that I am a robot. So if you have a solution for me please send it my way.</s><br /><br />Mr. Green can definitely write and he obviously is very well received by the audiences, if not how will he be a bestseller author, two movies produced based on his books already, heck they are probably even producing this one while I am writing this review. I don’t think there is anything atrocious, I just can’t connect and I feel very much bored while reading his stories. My only exception has been The Fault In Our Stars and his history youtube channel, <s>he has seriously saved me some grades.</s> But anyways let’s not make this personal.<br /><br /><b>Plot?</b><br /><br />Not consistent. It felt like a random stuff put together, finally distracting you from the actual point. I mean this would have been best if we were totally focused on the mental health aspect of the story, but suddenly this bounty hunter stuff was thrown at us, and it didn’t even have a worthy climax or anything. It felt dull.<br /><br /><b>Characters?</b> <br /><br />Couldn’t connect with anybody. As a teenager, I always end up with the sensation that I am reading adults (like not only in this book, but pretty much everything John Green has written), and it bothers me.<br /><br /><b>Aza:</b> I think people who have OCD could relate a lot to her and this whole book, I just couldn’t. But for that, I give 1,000 kudos, the representation a mental illness, but this just doesn't mean I loved this book. I really wanted more than just Aza’s perspective because I felt I couldn’t get anything from the book. Maybe this was the intention, but I basically hated it, because it felt like there was nothing going on or important to remember. She also made me realize I am really getting tired of the whole “psychologist suck they are just pricks who fake listening to us” because fuck I am freaking tired of all YA books not having good mental health help. <br /><br /><b>Davis:</b> Why did he even exist? I mean I felt he was the manic pixie dream character we always found in John Green’s characters. I liked he liked poetry, that’s about it. I honestly couldn’t even feel sorry for him and his dad plot. Yes, I have an ice heart. <br /><br /><b>Daisy: </b>Mmmmm…. How can I say this? Oh yeah, I didn’t like her. Again, she just was a terrible friend? As bad as Aza was to her, the fanfic part was too low my dear. Also, I haven’t watch star wars I don’t plan to watch it ever, and I was not the even minimum interested in her freaking Chubaka stories. <br /><br /><b>Relationship?</b> <br /><br />Why did it exist? H-O-N-E-S-T-L-Y. Please, someone, explain to me. There wasn’t even palpable attraction to start with, I couldn’t. I don’t even have words because there is basically nothing to talk about. <br /><br /><b>Writing?</b> <br /><br />Yeah some cool quotes, but I don’t emotionally connect, I felt bored.I really struggled, 258 pages felt like 1576868 pages. <br /><br />To not make this review completely negative here are some quotes I will keep. <s> Just know I still regret physically highlighting this book, I want my money back, sigh.</s> If the books were just this quotes it would have probably been 5 stars. <br /><br /><i>“But I was beginning to learn that your life is a story told.”<br /><br />“It’s a weird phrase in English, in love, like it’s a sea you drown in or a town you live in. You don’t get to be anything else-in friendship or in anger or in hope. All you can be is in love.”<br /><br />“I wanted to tell her that I was getting better because that was supposed to be the narrative of the illness: It was a hurdle you jumped over or a battle you won. Illness is a story told in the past.”<br /><br />“And we’re such language-based creatures that to some extent we cannot know what we cannot name. And so we assume it isn’t real. We refer to it with catch-all terms, like crazy or chronic pain, terms that both ostracize and minimize. The term chronic pain captures nothing of the grinding, constant, ceaseless, inescapable hurt. And the term crazy arrives at us with none of the terror or worry you live with. Nor do either of those terms connote the courage people in such pains exemplify, which is why I’d ask you to frame your mental health around a word other than crazy.”</i><br /><br />This book may have worked if my mental health was horrible, which I don't even know it means something good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7133387133455925925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2038007607" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2038007607" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2038007607?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780241335437" href="/book/show/35521513-turtles-all-the-way-down">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038007607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8162789416387132318"><i>
  <blockquote>“It's turtles all the way fucking down, Holmesy. You're trying to find the turtle at the bottom of the pile, but that's not how it works."<br/><br/>"Because it's turtles all the way down," I said again, feeling something akin to a spiritual revelation.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>my relationship with john green is hit and miss</b> and whether our relationship would end or continue all hinged on this book. folks, I'm pleased to say he's not cancelled yet. <br/><br/>Honestly, this book almost didn't feel like John Green. It does have staple Jo</span>
  <span id="freeText8162789416387132318" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“It's turtles all the way fucking down, Holmesy. You're trying to find the turtle at the bottom of the pile, but that's not how it works."<br /><br />"Because it's turtles all the way down," I said again, feeling something akin to a spiritual revelation.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>my relationship with john green is hit and miss</b> and whether our relationship would end or continue all hinged on this book. folks, I'm pleased to say he's not cancelled yet. <br /><br />Honestly, this book almost didn't feel like John Green. It does have staple John Green aspects, but at the same time it's <i>very thoughtful, very cohesive, and overall feels more mature</i>. I don't know what's changed between this book and TFIOS, but I really enjoyed the John Green we get in this book. Don't get me wrong: there's still a ridiculous amount of metaphor, simple, hyperbole, analogies, symbolism ect. I just think I happen to like those things. And metaphor is actually one of the only ways to describe what having a mental illness FEELS like. <br /><br />Turtles All the Way Down follows Aza Holmes, a 16 year old girl who's thrown into the investigation to find a missing billionaire, and is also trying to deal with her OCD. The billionaire plot kind of takes a backseat to the character work - this mostly focusses on Aza's mental health and her struggle with it. <br /><br /><b>the representation was both the hardest and best thing about this book</b> strong content warnings for this book because some things were kinda triggering, but at the same time the OCD rep is done .. really well. This is ownvoices representation and I think it's pretty clear how much John Green has put into putting forth an authentic and honest book about mental illness. John Green explores stigmatisation of MI, how it can become hard to balance your MI with your relationships, and the feeling of hopelessness when you're dealing with a mental illness that is spiralling out and out of control. I think it was great to see therapy, a positive discussion about medication and also the debunking of the "mentally ill people make better artists" trope thing (which sucks)<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Thoughts are only thoughts. They are not you, you belong to yourself even when your thoughts don't.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I also liked the subplots: the romance was nice, and I liked the discussions about privilege/wealth that came up. My favourite subplot was the disappearance of Davies Pickett Senior and how it was affecting his family. Even though this was character driven i liked how these plots played into the story, and I also liked that it was happening and didn't leave Aza as the "character who IS their MI" character. <br /><br />I also just liked how teenage-ery this was. I mean, Aza's best friend Daisy writes shippy Rey/Chewbaccaa star wars fanfiction on AO3 ? And also there's a line that literally says "he's probably some loser kylo ren stan" that's fucking hilarious and authentically teen. I really just enjoyed that there was so much fanfiction in this book.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“The thing about a spiral is, if you follow it inward, it never actually ends. It just keeps tightening, infinitely.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I just .. really thought this was nice. I thought it was well done. The representation is so so important. Like, guys we don't get good authentic MI rep like this that often. I really enjoyed the characters, I liked the writing and there was some lines and bits I really related to (after a good conversation you don't remember what you talked about, only how it made you feel being one of my favourites)<br /><br />There was also just ... none of the JG nonsense I didn't want. There was no dramatic romance with a nerd boy desperately trying to attain the girl. It was just .. good. I really enjoyed it so much more than I was expecting and I am going to gladly pick up more of this books in the future. YAY. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You're both the fire and the water that extinguishes it. You're the narrator, the protagonist, and the sidekick. You're the storyteller and the story told. You are somebody's something, but you are also your you.” </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8162789416387132318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2037659930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037659930" />
    <a title="☕️Jenny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39146653-jenny"><img alt="☕️Jenny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522871554p2/39146653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037659930?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☕️Jenny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☕️Jenny" href="/user/show/39146653-jenny">☕️Jenny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525555384" href="/book/show/15837671-turtles-all-the-way-down">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037659930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14661970247792035293"><i>"The thing about a spiral is, if you follow it inward, it never actually ends. It just keeps tightening, infinitely.”</i><br/><br/>(spoiler free) I started reading this book without knowing anything about the story or content. I've probably read the description when it was first announced that we would get another John Green book, but I honestly can't remember. I've read all John Green books so I thought I knew what I would sign up for reading this one. Well I was wrong.<br/><br/>My first thought after reading a couple</span>
  <span id="freeText14661970247792035293" style="display:none"><i>"The thing about a spiral is, if you follow it inward, it never actually ends. It just keeps tightening, infinitely.”</i><br /><br />(spoiler free) I started reading this book without knowing anything about the story or content. I've probably read the description when it was first announced that we would get another John Green book, but I honestly can't remember. I've read all John Green books so I thought I knew what I would sign up for reading this one. Well I was wrong.<br /><br />My first thought after reading a couple of pages? This book is hard to read.<br />And you know what? The book continues to be hard to read. And no, not because of bad or cheesy writing, bad characterization or a boring start into the book. No, this book is hard to read because it doesn't just focus heavily on a teen with mental health problems - no it actually describes the daily struggle of a 16 year old girl that deals with severe OCD and anxiety FROM HER OWN POINT OF VIEW.<br /><br />I've read a few books about people with OCD or/and anxiety before, but those always failed to describe what it truly feels like to basically fight your own brain. And then there's John Green finding words for something that I always found so hard to discuss. You can find words for almost everything you know. But imagine truly describing a mental illness. It doesn't help at all that you have to describe something that you can't even visualize yourself. But just because something can't be seen... doesn't make it any less real does it?<br /><br /><i>"One of the challenges with pain -physical or psychic - is that we can really only approach it through metaphor. It can't be represented the way a table or a body can. In some ways, pain is the opposite of language."</i><br /><br />OCD is the worst. Seriously. Imagine fighting with your own mind. You KNOW that what you're thinking isn't right, but your own brain works against you. You just HAVE to do something and it sickens you. You sicken yourself. Your own brain is your enemy. And still you do it over and over and over and over again. You fight against yourself and there can't be a winner. You make yourself angry. You make yourself cry. Shouldn't you be able to control what you're doing? Be able to fix yourself? Shouldn't you have a say concerning your body and mind? <br /><br />And lets not forget anxiety. Can you imagine how it feels to get so worried that you want to remove yourself from a situation before it even happened? To get a panic attack on a daily basis? To cry? And often you can't even explain WHY you're so anxious, because you don't even know? You're so afraid, so scared and you can't even find words to explain it. You just get stuck in your head and it feels like it will never get better?<br /><br /><i>"I would always be like this, always have this within me. There was no beating it. I would never slay the dragon because the dragon was also me. My self and the disease were knotted for life."</i><br /><br />And you know what's so weird about these problems? You often have good moments as well. Not just moments, sometimes days. You don't think about it, you have fun. You feel like you have control over what you're doing, over your life and even more important: Your thoughts. You go to school, meet your friends, have conversations. All these things that we take for granted. And then it comes back. Full force. You worry. You think. You get stuck in your head. You argue with yourself. You try to fight, but at the end you still lose. Any you know what? It feels so much worse because you just got a glimpse of what your life could be like.<br /><br /><i>"I think and I think and I think."</i><br /><br />Let's not forget the reaction of the people in your life or at least the reaction that you fear you'll get after telling people about your mental illness. You don't want to be called crazy. You don't want to be called an attention seeker. You don't want them to feel helpless, because they can't help you. You don't want to explain to people that No you just can't "stay positive and everything will be better tomorrow." The thing with many mental health issues is: It never goes away entirely. You can get help and it can get better. But that's a process and sure as hell won't be achieved overnight.<br /><br />So at the end what remains to be said? Did the book get easier to read for me? No, it didn‘t. Should it get easier? No, absolutely not. Mental health problems are often too easily ignored. Step for step people start to recognize them as real diseases but it needs books like this to show people the truth behind a name like "anxiety" that fails to show the severeness of the problem it titles. What John Green does in this book is easily explained but still oh so complex. He finds words for these mental illnesses without actually describing all of the medical basics we so often get to hear. He doesn't just dump information on the reader that you can easily find on Wikipedia or is just another google search away. He actually narrates how the daily life of a person dealing with anxiety/OCD is. He doesn't hide anything. And you know what? That's what makes the book so hard to read. Because hearing about something and actually experiencing it are two different things.<br /><br />And you know what? I want to thank John Green. Thank you for writing a book that features mental health and brings the subject to a broad audience. And while my review (mental health rant?) focused on the worse parts, you also showed that no one is alone and everyone can get help. There are things that will always be more difficult for people like John Green, his character and Aza, me &amp; the many people who also deal with mental illnesses daily, BUT we're not living for the disease, we're living for the light in between. It may seem like you're in this dark place forever, but you're not alone and it will get better. To come back to the quote from the beginning: "The thing about a spiral is, if you follow it inward, it never actually ends. It just keeps tightening, infinitely." That may be true, but the following quote also is:<br /><br /><i>"Spirals grow infinitely small the farther you follow them inward, but they also grow infinitely large the farther you follow them out.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14661970247792035293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2198047520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2198047520" />
    <a title="may ❀" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49148508-may"><img alt="may ❀" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562443036p2/49148508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2198047520?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ❀" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ❀" href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=200-pgs">200-pgs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=binged">binged</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=decent">decent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49148508-may?shelf=real-problems">real-problems</a>,
